Popular Lectures

Yue Fei's Childhood

— Li Jizhen

—He never forgot to be a good person who was both "loyal and filial"—

Yue Wumu was born on the fifteenth day of the second month of the second year of Chongning during the reign of Emperor Huizong of the Song Dynasty (year 203 of the Christian era) in Tangyin County, Xiangzhou Prefecture, Henan. His father, named He, was a renowned scholar who often said, "Even if one is unfortunate enough to be born in a chaotic world, and is just an ordinary person without power or courage, one must never forget the nation and only seek to survive. Many people misunderstand Mr. Kongming's 'Seeking only to preserve life in troubled times, and not seeking fame among the lords,' thinking that being able to survive in troubled times is already a blessing, so why be overly ambitious? In fact, Mr. Kongming's 'preserving life' was about working hard to cultivate morality and learning. When his morality and learning matured, he would seize the opportunity to come out and work for the salvation of the country and its people. Look at him when he came out of his thatched hut, wasn't he accomplished in both literary talent and military strategy? This shows that when he was in the thatched hut, he was not only not 'preserving life,' but also working very hard. My ambition is to learn from Mr. Kongming." Therefore, Yue He worked very hard, either studying literature or practicing martial arts every day. Seeing the emperor's blindness and the officials' treachery in the court, he knew it would be difficult to meet a wise ruler like Kongming. However, he still refused to be discouraged and planned that if he was unsuccessful, he would pass on what he had learned to his son, and his son would pass it on to his grandson, generation after generation. He believed that his ambition and talent to stabilize the country would eventually be realized one day. He also thought, "To have good descendants, I can't rely on myself alone, I must find a good wife." He patiently chose, and finally got a beautiful, intelligent, and virtuous woman named Yao to be his wife.

This virtuous couple got along very well together. Yue He had no elders above him and no children below him, and his wife was thrifty, so the household expenses were very low. He had thousands of acres of fertile land, and most of the annual income was used to help the poor people in the neighborhood. They were happy to have a small family, firstly because they could save money and cultivate a frugal style, and secondly because they could save time, allowing his wife to spend half of her housekeeping time with him reciting scriptures and history.

Such happy and meaningful days passed particularly quickly, and in the blink of an eye, ten years had passed. Wumu was born on the tenth anniversary of Yue He and his wife's marriage. At that time, Yue He was already forty, and his wife was almost thirty. They finally got the little baby they had been waiting for for many years, and they were so happy that words could not describe it. They firmly believed that if they taught him properly, this beautiful jade would surely become a useful person. They placed all their hopes on their son and tried their best to teach him. They wanted to give him a good name that was meaningful, but they couldn't think of one after thinking for three days. It just so happened that the "Tangbinghui" (noodles feast) was to be held on the third day after the birth, according to custom. Yue He had become impoverished due to his benevolence and generosity over the past ten years, but he still wanted to take advantage of this "Tangbinghui" to invite the poor people in the neighborhood to have a good meal. He got up before dawn that day and ran to his good friend Zhou Tong, who lived ten miles away, to borrow money. If he took the main road from his home to Zhou's, it would take half a day, but if he took the mountain road, he could save most of the time. Because he was afraid of missing the time to invite guests, he preferred to take the mountain road, even though it was harder. As he walked, he thought about what to name his son. When he reached the top of the mountain, the sky suddenly turned completely dark, and the piercing wind was unbearably cold. Yue He exclaimed, "Now is mid-spring, even if it's going to rain, there shouldn't be such a cold wind. What kind of disaster is this?" After a while, the weather suddenly changed again, the sky was clear and the air was fresh, orioles were singing under the willows, and butterflies were dancing in front of the flowers. What beautiful scenery! Strangely enough, he stretched his neck and looked around, and saw a huge bird flying over from afar, covering the sky and the sun. Its momentum was majestic and it was a very magnificent sight. Therefore, he decided to call his beloved son "Fei."

He got the money and came back to tell his wife about what he had seen and how he named his son. His wife happily said, "I remember when the little baby was about to be born, there was a very loud sound on the roof. I asked you to go and see what was going on, and you said you only saw a big bird flying away in the distance, and nothing else. As soon as you finished speaking, my stomach started to hurt. What you saw today might be the same one as the other day. What is it? Could it be the Peng bird that Zhuangzi spoke of? How about we give him another name, "Pengju"?" Yue He listened and agreed very much.

Yue's wife's family was in Neihuang County, Daming Prefecture, Hebei. They were originally a wealthy scholarly family, but they had declined in recent years. There was an old mother and a younger brother in the family, who lived by farming. When Yue Fei was almost a month old, his mother's family sent someone to take her home, saying that the old lady missed her so much that she was sick, and wanted her to return to Neihuang to visit her parents. Yue's wife was a filial daughter. Hearing that her mother was sick, she couldn't wait to have wings to fly home and serve her mother. Yue He sympathized with her and told her to take her son and the messenger to leave two days earlier. He would have to finish his son's full-month celebration before he could leave home, because he had already invited many relatives and friends from afar to come to drink喜酒(wedding/celebration) on the full-month day, and he didn't have time to decline them one by one, so he had to stay at home to entertain them himself. Yue's wife returned to her mother's home. The old lady was very happy to see her daughter and her newborn grandson after a long separation, and her illness improved a lot.

That day, the mother and daughter talked happily until late at night. Unexpectedly, there was a great flood in Neihuang in the middle of the night, and the whole county turned into a swamp. Yue's wife's younger brother staggered in and said to her, "Sister, the flood is here. I have to take care of the old lady. You have to find a way to escape by yourself. I can't take care of you." As he spoke, he carried his mother on his back and walked to a higher place. Yue's wife hurriedly picked up Yue Fei and went out to find a way to survive. The water rose higher and higher, and soon it had submerged her thighs. Yue's wife didn't know what to do. Suddenly, she touched a large water vat floating beside her. Without thinking, she sat in the vat, tightly holding Yue Fei in her arms, and listened attentively to the flying sounds and the sound of the water all around, mixed with the cries of refugees near and far. The water vat drifted to the shore with the current, and Yue's wife and son survived. When the water receded at dawn, people saw them and everyone said it was a miracle. Yue's wife's mother and younger brother were also fortunate to survive. The mother, daughter, and siblings were very happy to see each other. Yue He rushed over as soon as he heard the news of the flood and took his wife's family to Tangyin. The next day was Yue Fei's full-month celebration. Everyone was drinking celebration wine of family reunion, while shedding tears of pain and grief.

Time passed quickly, and several years passed. Yue's wife's mother and younger brother had already returned to Neihuang. Yue Fei had grown into an exceptionally clever and sensible child. Although Yue He and his wife liked him very much, they were unwilling to indulge him because they hoped that he would become a useful person. When Yue Fei was four years old, his father asked him to go to the study to study. Yue Fei was both smart and hardworking. By the time he was twelve years old, he had already finished reading the Four Books, Five Classics, and the works of various philosophers and historians. At this time, Yue He could barely make a living by farming. Yue Fei brought food to the fields every day, and when he saw his father weeding and plowing the fields, sweating like rain, and working very hard, he wanted to stay in the fields to work for his father. His father, because he was young and afraid of delaying his study time, always coaxed him with gentle words, saying that farming was the most interesting and least tiring work. He understood his father's meaning and didn't dare to argue with his father, so he had to come back with tears in his eyes. When he got home, he was afraid that his mother would see his sad face, so he wiped away his tears before he dared to enter the house. But he always felt that it was a shame and embarrassing for a son to be unable to support his parents.

One day, he was sitting in the study, and he thought of his father working hard in the fields again. He saw the piles of books in front of him and couldn't help but sigh, "What's the use of reading ten thousand volumes of books if a son can't support his parents?" He thought of what the ancients said, "The father chops wood, but the son cannot carry the load." He couldn't help but cry out loud.

Yue's wife was a smart woman. Although Yue Fei didn't dare to show any signs of unhappiness in front of her, she had already seen through Yue Fei's concerns. She just didn't say it, and paid attention to observing her son's actions. That day, she was mending clothes in the house when she suddenly heard her son crying. She quickly put down her needle and thread and went to the study to see what was going on. When Yue Fei saw his mother, he knew he couldn't hide it, and he couldn't help but kneel down. Yue's wife quickly helped him up, used her sleeve to wipe away his tears, and asked softly, "My son, what unhappy things do you have at such a young age? Can you tell Mother?"

When Yue Fei heard his mother's words, he couldn't help but cry again. After a while, he said intermittently, "Mother—I... I bring Father's food to the fields every day, and I see... I see him working too hard. I can't bear to let Father suffer like this. I want to work for him, but he... he won't let me, so I don't feel good. But I still don't understand that I am an unfilial person. Just now I thought of what the ancients said, 'The father chops wood, but the son cannot carry the load.' Then I knew I was unfilial, because Father is farming and I'm not doing anything. Isn't that unfilial? I hate unfilial and disloyal people the most. How can you not hate myself?" As he said this, he cried again, and said as he cried, "Mother—I don't want to be an unfilial son. Can you think of an idea for me?"

When Yue's wife heard her son's words, she was filled with mixed feelings of sadness and joy. She was sad because the family was poor, which exhausted her husband and worried her son. She was happy that her son, who was so young, was so filial, could study, and knew how to be a person. Although she cherished Yue Fei's health, she liked Yue Fei's virtues even more. She wanted to help him become a filial son. So she said to Yue Fei:

"My son, get up! Mother has thought of an idea for you. It's true, 'The father chops wood, but the son cannot carry the load' is unfilial. But you are still young. Since you are determined to help your father, wait until Mother tells him and asks him to let you work in the fields."

Yue Fei went to farm on the first day. He was enthusiastic and worked hard, and worked better than anyone else. At first, he still needed his father to teach him, but later he was able to do everything independently. He worked during the day and studied at night, and he didn't waste any time. He didn't have money to buy lamp oil, so he went to the fields to collect firewood, burned it in the yard at night, and sat in front of the firewood pile to read. He did the same in summer. The firewood smoke blackened his face and his clothes were soaked with sweat. He would only wash himself clean when it was dawn. The villagers all praised him, saying that he was a hard-working and filial son. A Mr. Li liked Yue Fei so much that he wanted to marry his only daughter to him as his daughter-in-law.

Yue Fei had grown to be eighteen years old, and his learning and character had made amazing progress. He was very calm and rarely spoke. But seeing his upright and solemn attitude, everyone knew that he was a child of integrity. Because he was willing to move, his strength was very great, and he could draw a strong bow and pull a strong crossbow. He liked to read widely, and his favorite books were the Zuo Zhuan and Sun Tzu's Art of War.

That year, after the autumn harvest, because it was a bumper year, the farmers were celebrating together. Yue He and his wife were invited to drink wine at a neighbor's house, leaving Yue Fei and his daughter-in-law to guard the house. Yue Fei sent his parents to the neighbor's house, came back, closed the bamboo fence gate, pulled the bow and practiced archery in the yard, changed his clothes, and sat on the grass in the sun, loudly reciting Sun Tzu's Art of War.

Unexpectedly, his father's good friend Zhou Tong happened to come to visit. Zhou Tong was a famous scholar from Shaanxi, who was accomplished in both literature and martial arts, and had the divine skill of good archery. Because his only son died in the border fighting against the Liao, he was too heartbroken to live in his hometown, so he specially came to Tangyin, Henan, to be a hermit. He rarely socialized, but he especially liked Yue He's heroism and righteousness. When Yue Fei was five years old, he left Tangyin and traveled around. He knew that Yue Fei was an extraordinary person, and after wandering for thirteen years, he finally wanted to return to Tangyin to see this smart child. In the thirteen years, everything in Yue's Village had changed. The small green willows that he left had now grown into trees that could be embraced. The children who used to stare at strangers with curiosity still followed him around, but none of them were the same faces. He remembered that Yue's house was not far from here. He was just about to find someone to ask for directions when he suddenly heard clear reading sounds not far ahead, which were very pleasant. He could tell that it was a young boy's voice, and he was reading Sun Tzu. He thought, "Whose family has such a promising child? Could it be the son of a general?" He followed the sound of the reading to the bamboo fence and recognized that this was Yue's house. He was just about to knock on the door when the dog's barking had already startled Yue Fei. Yue Fei saw a heroic and kind old man standing outside the fence gate. He hurriedly opened the door and respectfully invited the elder in. He respectfully asked for his name and only then did he know that this was his father's good friend Zhou Tong, who had come from thousands of miles away to visit. He hurriedly went to the neighbor's house to inform his father. The good friends were reunited, and everyone was infinitely happy.

Zhou Tong highly valued Yue Fei and was determined to pass on his talents and archery skills to him. Yue He knew that Zhou Tong was a great master and was afraid of missing the opportunity, so he immediately ordered his son to come and worship him as his teacher. That night, the Yue family held a grand banquet to welcome Zhou Tong, and the next day, Zhou Tong began to teach.

At that time, Zhou Tong was already old. He knew that he had been sad for half his life and would not live long. He was afraid that his knowledge would be lost, so he taught his disciples wholeheartedly day and night. Yue Fei also respected his teacher very much. He did whatever his teacher told him to do. He had a firm heart and strong spirit, and his body was strong. He didn't feel tired even if he used his brain and strength all day long. The more he learned, the more motivated he became. After learning archery for two years, he could draw a strong bow of three hundred catties and shoot a strong crossbow of eight stones. He had learned all of Zhou Tong's skills and could shoot with both hands. Yue Fei was grateful to Zhou Tong for teaching him so painstakingly, and he pitied him for having no children in his old age. He intended to serve him as if he were his father, so that he could live his later years in peace and happiness. Unexpectedly, Zhou Tong did not receive any reward from Yue Fei. He died after being sick for a few days.

Yue Fei held his benefactor's body and cried bitterly. He buried Zhou Tong in his hometown so that he could come to sweep his tomb often. He picked up a book and thought of his teacher, often sighing at the book. He held a bow and thought of his teacher, and couldn't help but shed tears as he shot the crossbow. Every first and fifteenth day of the month, he would definitely visit Zhou Tong's tomb to worship him, and he never changed the date, rain or shine. When Yue He saw how righteous he was, he couldn't help but praise him:

"Son! If you are ever used by the world, you will definitely be a person who sacrifices yourself for the country and dies for righteousness."

Yue Fei listened and couldn't say anything for a long time. His father said again:

"Son, the national crisis is getting worse day by day. Your father is old, and the hope of saving the country and its people rests on your shoulders. There are not few loyal ministers and righteous people in ancient and modern times. Son, I hope you will be the most pure and complete one."

Yue Fei said, "Dad, I will always remember your teachings today. I must be the most pure and complete one."

At that time, Song's diplomatic policy of using Jin to drive away Liao had turned into inviting a wolf into the house. The Jin people captured Yanjing, and not only refused to return the lost land, but also planned to invade Song. Emperor Huizong was a useless person who only sought his own pleasure and knew nothing about diplomacy and national affairs. He ended up with both foreign and domestic troubles breaking out, and he couldn't find a way to clean things up. Yue He knew that this was the time for righteous people to make contributions and serve the country, so he wanted Yue Fei to join the army. So he took the opportunity to say to Yue Fei, "Son, if you want to save the country and its people, now is the opportunity. Go and join the army."

Yue Fei was determined to join the army, but he was afraid that his parents would have no one to take care of them at home, so he hesitated and dared not agree immediately. Fortunately, his father knew the reason why he couldn't make up his mind, so he quickly said to him, "Son, saving the country is much more important than serving your parents. Saving the country and serving your parents are two sides of the same coin. If the country is destroyed, your parents will lose their support. What's the use of just talking about serving your parents? Besides, we don't necessarily need you by our side right now. The remaining food at home can support us for a year if we are frugal. Your daughter-in-law can replace you in taking care of us in the morning and evening. Son, make up your mind and go!"

At this time, Liu Xuanfu of Zhending was recruiting soldiers. Yue Fei told his parents and went to enlist. Yue Fei received an order to suppress bandits as soon as he arrived at the camp. He led a hundred soldiers and destroyed two major bandits in Xiangzhou, each with tens of thousands of people. His superiors were about to promote him when he received a letter saying that his father was seriously ill. He rushed home without caring about anything. Yue He was already seriously ill, his face turned gray and white, and he was lying in bed, unable to move his limbs. His head was facing out of the house, and his eyes were wide open, as if waiting for something. When he heard that Yue Fei had returned, his head suddenly lifted up and he reached out for someone to help him up. The people in the family were rejoicing that his illness had taken a turn for the better, but who knew that he could only say one sentence, "Son, you're back!" before falling back dead. Yue Fei and his mother held the body and cried as if they were dying. Yue Fei was afraid of hurting his mother too much, so he endured his tears and comforted her while taking care of the funeral arrangements. After a hundred days, the funeral was completed according to etiquette.

At that time, Yue Fei was already twenty years old. He didn't make any decisions on his own. He reported everything to his loving mother. Yue's wife allowed him to observe mourning at home, working in the fields for half a day every day, and spending the rest of his time practicing martial arts and studying history. Yue Fei never forgot his father's last teachings and was determined to fulfill his father's unfinished ambition. He often thought, "I heard that 'the ancients sought loyal ministers from the homes of filial sons.' Before becoming a purely loyal minister, one should first become a purely filial son." He was originally a person of utmost filial piety by nature, and now he was even more determined to reach the realm of pure and complete filial piety. Countless evil people and wicked sons from far and near changed their ways after hearing of his good deeds.

At that time, the rebel Yang Yao was causing trouble in Huguang. He heard people say that Yue Fei was a talented person and wanted to recruit him. He sent people to Tangyin with humble words and generous gifts to invite Yue Fei. Yue Fei sternly and righteously rebuked the messengers and sent them back. He then told Yue's wife about everything that had happened and knelt at his mother's knees, weeping and saying:

"Mother! Your child has been taught by both parents since childhood, and I have never forgotten to be a good person who is both 'loyal and filial.' I think everyone should understand this honest and upright heart. Your child doesn't understand why someone would dare to invite your child to be a traitor who betrays the country and abandons his parents. Could it be that your child has done something wrong that makes people look down on me?"

"My son, don't be sad, and don't despise yourself too much. Even saints cannot avoid the losses you have suffered today. You must only make your determination even firmer, and be even more careful in your actions. When evil people see your steadfastness, they will naturally not dare to invade you." As Yue's wife said this, she suddenly thought of a way to make her son's determination even stronger. She ordered Yue Fei to bring the incense table, light the incense and candles, and ordered Yue Fei to take off his shirt and kneel reverently to the sky. She pulled out a small silver hairpin from her hair and tattooed the four words "Serve the Country with Utmost Loyalty" on Yue Fei's back. As she tattooed the words, she told her son:

"Son! Mother is getting old and may leave you sooner or later. There are many bad people in troubled times, and young people are most easily deceived. I'm afraid that as soon as I let go, you will forget your family teachings and learn bad things from others. Therefore, I tattooed the four words "Serve the Country with Utmost Loyalty" on your back, so that you will always remember Mother's teachings and take on the responsibility of "Serving the Country with Utmost Loyalty."

Their sincerity dominated everything, so the loving mother endured the pain of tattooing her back, and the son didn't feel any pain at all.

Later, Yue Fei joined the army, defeated the Jin soldiers, and saved the Song Dynasty from destruction. Because he wanted to achieve "pure completeness" and "utmost loyalty," he ultimately sacrificed himself for the country. The reason why he had such great talent and supreme virtue was entirely due to his good upbringing in his youth.

Publishing World

"Collected Education Broadcast Lectures"

— Yingfu

Volume 1: Public Education

The educational broadcast lectures organized by the Ministry of Education began in October of the 24th year of the Republic (1935). These lectures were divided into two aspects: one was about secondary education, and the other was about public education. Both were held simultaneously until the winter vacation of last year, when they were temporarily suspended. Here, the first volume of the Collected Education Broadcast Lectures (Secondary Education), which we are about to introduce, is the first aspect of the educational broadcast lectures held by the Ministry of Education last year, edited by the ministry and recently published by the Commercial Press.

The motivation and process of the Ministry of Education organizing educational lectures has already been explained by the Minister of Education in the first lecture, so there is no need for us to repeat it. What we want to talk about here is a little feeling that we had after reading the lecture collection. First, let's talk about the classification of the speeches. The content of the lecture collection is divided into four categories: (1) Youth Training; (2) Subject Lectures; (3) Education Lectures; and (4) Current Affairs Lectures. Such a method of material distribution is not wrong in terms of the above four items. However, what we consider a minor dissatisfaction is the distribution of the quantity of speeches under the four items. For example, the speeches on youth training, which is in the first category, should have been particularly emphasized according to the needs of secondary school students, and their length should have accounted for at least half or one-third of the entire collection. However, in reality, there are only four articles, which occupy the smallest position compared with the speeches in other categories. For example, the speeches on subject lectures, which is in the second category, should have been second only to the first category, but in reality, they occupy as many as eighteen articles. This improper distribution of materials is certainly not the responsibility of the editors, but should be the responsibility of the organization that organized the educational broadcast lectures. In other words, the Education Department should pay attention to the youth training category in the distribution of lecture materials, or give equal importance to this category and the subject lecture category. Furthermore, there is another small flaw in the quantity of content, which is the omission of materials. For example, in the youth training category, there should be a speech on the student movement, explaining clearly the meaning, history, past mistakes, and the path that should be taken now. Also, school unrest is also a very important issue, and there should be a speech by a famous educator, giving a correct answer to schools and students. Also, in the education lecture category, only one lecture involved the service problem of normal school students, but there was no lecture on the problems of further education, employment, and unemployment of general secondary school graduates. These are all the points that we consider to be lacking.

Next, let us talk about the quality of the content of this lecture collection. In this aspect, we cannot find any dissatisfaction. All thirty-four lectures collected in the collection can be said to have their own outstanding and correct views, either giving guidance on the cultivation of secondary school students, or providing assistance to their studies, or expanding their common knowledge. This is what we think is most beneficial to them. From this point, we can affirm that the educational lectures held last year were very successful and effective.

Now, let's cite the advantages of two lectures to prove the above praise. For example, the elements of modern youth's cultivation of learning and virtue, as spoken by Luo Jialun, has quite outstanding and correct ideas. He put forward three elements that must be possessed by modern youth in their cultivation: (1) the scientific spirit of seeking knowledge; (2) the living habits of soldiers; (3) the competitive ethics of athletes. Furthermore, he further divided the second element into four points, namely (incomplete)

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Random Talk

The Death of a Servant

— Wu Ci

Some nouns are unremarkable to the ears of Shanghainese, but bewildering to outsiders. For example, "servant." Even the most erudite scholars probably couldn't unearth its origins in ancient texts. Yet, in Shanghai, even women and children know what kind of person it refers to.

Though "servant" is a common term in Shanghai, its commonness does not diminish its baseness. Those who call others "servant" adopt an air of superiority. And the servant, upon hearing a call, would hastily and respectfully respond with "Yes, Master!" This is especially true in foreign firms or the homes of wealthy foreigners. They often employ Chinese servants, primarily because they appreciate their submissive demeanor and that respectful "Yes, Master!"

However, once one's status becomes lowly, one's character seems unable to elevate. The reason is simple: noble people do noble deeds, while the base naturally become vulgar. This isn't necessarily due to their inherent nature, but rather the "defense in depth" strategy of the noble class. A vast chasm is clearly drawn between servants and masters. Those on the servant's side are often labeled as "vulgar and filthy," while those on the master's side are always associated with "morality" and so on. This can be demonstrated with an example:

"Chen Yaosheng, a local man working as a servant for a certain foreigner, was suspected of stealing an electric heater that the foreigner had lost a few days ago. The foreigner dismissed Chen, and Chen subsequently committed suicide by poison. After the discovery, he was rushed to the hospital, but the treatment was ineffective, and he died immediately... The court prosecutor determined that Chen Yaosheng died from poisoning and instructed his family to arrange the funeral."

Of course, in the eyes of foreigners, the suicide of a mere servant is less stimulating than Romeo's suicide in Shakespeare's tragedy "Romeo and Juliet." Moreover, suicide is the act of the weak, so there's no need for sympathy. The fact that they didn't attribute terms like "discovered conscience and died of shame" to Chen Yaosheng is already generous enough.

Although we do not advocate suicide, we cannot help but feel moved by the death of Chen Yaosheng. This "feeling" arises from the position of servants and their lowly duties. Servants generally lack much knowledge, which is a fact. However, lacking knowledge does not necessarily make someone vulgar, which is also a fact. And precisely because their minds are simple, they retain a bit of innocence in this hypocritical and cunning society. This innocence provides "intellectuals" with plenty of laughable material in their actions. For example, being falsely accused of theft is not a reason for suicide. If we were to put ourselves in his place, suppose the one who lost something (certainly not an electric heater) was the servant, and the master was suspected of theft. Then, the master would either dismiss it with a "haha" or slap the servant with his giant hand. And the onlookers in society would express a sense of justice and speak up in unison:

"How could he be a thief? Are you trying to frame him out of sheer boredom!"

Under such circumstances, even if the master really likes to steal, his top hat and formal attire would still be respected. Poor Chen Yaosheng, he didn't know these things. He didn't know that in this society, the more upper-class a person is, the more they engage in theft. Not only is their mask never pierced after they do it, but even if it is, they still let others laugh and scold as they please, and the gentleman continues to be himself. Fortunately, many so-called "righteous" people in society are allied with these "gentlemen." When they see the gentleman's mask about to be pierced, they will unite to cover it up because they know that if the lips are gone, the teeth will be cold, and they also fear that the rabbit's death will cause the fox to grieve.

Yangjia Port

— Yunhai

Autumn. Without towering waves, the sea cannot pile up great mountains. Looking from afar, it seems only small waves chase and play, which is quite endearing.

Two or three sea eagles soar in mid-air. Their thick wings move vigorously as if keeping time, embellishing the entire blue-green sky with peace and gentleness. When their sharp and keen eyes spot the schools of fish chasing each other in groups of three or five, their steel-hard beaks point downward, and the weight of their bodies is unbalanced again. They fly down quickly, splashing lightly on the water’s surface, catching their prey with a gentle peck. Then, with a turn of the head and a squeak, they shoot straight into the clouds. Such flight is extremely swift and agile, so fast that even the human eye is dazzled.

Over there, protruding behind two embrace-like small peaks is a naturally dangerous islet – this is Yangjia Port. Many fishermen have buried their happy lives here for the sake of livelihood. At the same time, several years ago, many lucky people relied on this mountain to make a fortune and put on silk clothes. However, that was in the past. Now, this desolate natural fishing net has had its path cut off by the fishermen upstream of the West River. Whole schools of fish rarely come to this aging Yangjia Port anymore. At this time, only small sailboats that have split up and make a living by salvaging are left.

On that phosphorous-nitrate shore, where the waves crash, there are often three or five half-naked fisherwomen, opening a large net, facing the shallow water. Spending about

Page 22

the time it takes for a bell to strike, they stretch out their poor, greedy eyes towards that tattered fishing net, pinning on a hope.

"Pah! That damn ×! Yellow plague!"

The net only catches struggling jumping river shrimp, along with a few silvery white small fish. Thus, they are disappointed, and they curse resentfully from the bottom of their hearts.

Slap – shush shush

A dark wave, surging from who knows where, crashes violently onto the cliffs. Unable to stand firm, she is knocked down. Her body leans to one side, and the rope tangles, but those walking beside her quickly pull it taut, finally managing to steady her footing and stand up. She mutters and curses:

"What gale is coming from that ocean? It's hitting your old lady so hard! Late autumn, right at high tide..."

"Sister-in-law, I don't think this is a good sign? Look, the sky over there is covered by a pile of dark clouds. I'm afraid the wind and rain will rush over here in no time!"

The young sister-in-law advises the sister-in-law who can't stand steadily, as if she's full of experience. The sister-in-law then regains her senses. Her mouth opens and closes in panic, and then she gasps as if taking a breath:

"Let's go! Let's go! The headwind is no joke. I'm afraid we won't make it back to the village! That damn ×:…"

Over there, the small sailboats that came with them are all craning their necks. Everyone is hurrying to haul in their nets. Once the nets are collected, the people get on board. Then they have to furl the sails - nine out of ten sails will fall in the wind. Thus, they frantically and chaotically yell and call out. The tranquility of just now has been frightened away to who knows where. The dark clouds have spread their wings and covered over. A burst of darkness scares people into even more chaos. The sea eagles in the sky have disappeared to who knows where. All that remains here is terror, panic, and a fear like the approach of a great disaster.

Exhausting their strength, these small sailboats, like fish on a string, struggle close to the opposite shore.

"Yo ay yo, ya wei... Ah, yo, ay yo..."

It seems like a cry of despair, and it seems like the moan of the weak. Here, it is drowned out by this low, depressed, life-seeking, upward melody.

Woo woo! Woo!

The wind gradually gathers from all directions, howling demonstratively. The dark clouds, swirling in the air like a vicious bird, have now completely covered the sea. Everything has sunk into the gloomy atmosphere. The autumn waves stirred up by the wind are bigger than everything else. Surging up from a small hill, forming giant waves higher than the boats, like a magician's hand, cruelly and wantonly teasing these small sailboats struggling for survival. The bow of the small boat collides with the greedy, insatiable wave mountain that is opening its mouth, and is unnaturally thrown into the air, and then unnaturally thrown down again. It rolls and tumbles in this up-and-down manner.

The people on the boat are as solemn as Buddha statues. They rely on their experience to fight against the fate of death. The helmsman is steady and determined. The one rowing the oars at the front of the boat now seems to have completely lost consciousness, only knowing to strain the red veins in his forehead as he rows. The young children have also forgotten to laugh and play, and are scooping buckets and buckets of bilge water with an adult air.

Rain also attacks from all directions. Hitting people's faces, hands, and skin, it is a spicy, stinging pain. However, the struggle, the people are singing about this courageous fight.
